NO. 21-CI-004985 JEFFERSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT

DIVISION FIVE (5) JUDGE MARY SHAW ANELLA NOBLE PLAINTIFF V. VIRGINIA P. SEWELL; STATE FARM MUTUAL INSURANCE COMPANY; & UNKNOWN DRIVER DEFENDANTS

PLAINTIFF’S RESPONSES TO DEFENDANT VIRGINIA P. SEWELL’s INTERROGATORIES ANDREQUESTS FOR PRODUCTION OF DOCUMENTS

Come the Plaintiff, Anella Noble, by counsel, and responds to the Interrogatories and Requestfor

Production of Documents propounded by the Defendant, Virginia P. Sewell.

GENERAL OBJECTIONS

To the extent any instruction contained in Defendant’s Discovery request exceeds the language orscope

of the Kentucky Rules of Civil Procedure it is objected to and will not be complied with.

To the extent any request calls for information which is protected under the work product doctrine or attorney client privilege is objected to and will not be answered. Nothing in these responses shall be

deemed a waiver of work product doctrine or attorney-client privilege.

These answers and responses reflect the current state of Plaintiff's knowledge concerning the documents requested and questions asked. These responses are given without prejudice to the Plaintiff's right to use or rely at any time, including trial, subsequently discovered information or documents omitted from these responses by providing information in response to Defendant’s discovery requests, Plaintiff does notconcede that any information is relevant, material, or admissible.

Page 1 of 18




Plaintiff reserves all rights to object to the admissibility of any evidence.

Plaintiff reserves all rights to supplement, change, or amend any response, calculation, description, or

amount contained in any response herein.

INTERROGATORY NO. 5:

Provide the complete name and address of each and every individual or entity by which Plaintiff has been employed for the past ten (10) years and the date of such employment. worked per year and the reason for termination of employment.

ANSWER:

Objection. Irrelevant. Plaintiff ’s employment history is irrelevant to the subject matter of this matter, and the information sought is not reasonably calculated to lead to the

discovery of admissible evidence.

ofthis lawsuit and not calculated to lead to the discovery of admissible evidence.

INTERROGATORY NO. 9:

the accident, which is the subject of this litigation, and for each, supply the date of recovery (if

applicable) and your present condition relative to such injury.

ANSWER:

Objection, Plaintiff has limited knowledge as to the extent of her injuries suffered as a result of the accident as the Plaintiff is not a medical professional and has limited

medical knowledge.

Without waiving said objections, Plaintiff request the Defendant to rely upon the

medical records of licensed medical professional for this answer.

Plaintiff further states that she suffers from tightness & discomfort in her neck, shoulders and lower back throughout the day. Her neck & shoulder pain is sporadic. Her low back pain is often and causes discomfort when laying down or when walking.

INTERROGATORY NO. 19:

AN

Identify all persons known or reasonably thought by you, your agents, or other representatives, to have been a witness to the occurrence described in the Complaint, and state whether you obtained any statements from said witnesses and the facts or knowledge of each such witness is believed to possess.

ER:

Objection, Attorney work-product. This interrogatory seeks premature disclosure of

witnesses.

Without waiving said objection, the Plaintiff has not decided on which, if any, witnesses may be called at trial; insofar as this interrogatory seeks to ascertain the identity, writings, and opinions of plaintiff ’s witnesses who have been retained or utilized to date solely as an advisor or consultant, it is violative of the work-product

privilege.

took recorded statements as a matter of procedure.

INTERROGATORY NO. 25:

Describe each and every fact which supports the allegation that Defendant Sewell “negligently and carelessly entrusted said vehicle to the unknown driver”.

ANSWER: Plaintiff states the officer on the scene identified that the unknown driver as Defendant

Sewell’s significant other and only after attempting to report the vehicle stolen and the officer advising her that the ignition had not been damaged did Defendant Sewell

Page 11 of 18




change her story and advised she had a spare key but has not been able to locate that key

for a while.

Please refer to Louisville Metro Police Department Report # 80-21000497

INTERROGATORY NO. 26:

Describe each and every fact upon which you based your allegation that “Defendant Sewell knew or should have known that the [Defendant Driver] would operate the vehicle in a careless

manner.”

ANSWER:

Plaintiff states the [Defendant Driver] was presented as Defendant Sewell’s significant

other whom she would have intimate knowledge of.

INTERROGATORY NO. 27:

> «

Describe each and every fact which supports your allegation that Defendant Sewell’s “negligent

entrustment of the vehicle was a substantial factor in causing the Plaintiffs injuries.”

ANSWER:

Plaintiff states that if Defendant Sewell had not been “unable to locate her spare key’, Defendant Sewell could have ensured the operator of the vehicle at the time of the accident was of sound mind and would not have caused the accident subject of this

litigation.

INTERROGATORY NO. 28:

Identify the driver whom you allege was operating the vehicle involved in the motor vehicle

collision described in the Plaintiff's complaint.

ANSWER:

Officers at the scene were able to locate photos of Virginia Sewell’s significant other via social media, the photos were presented to and confirmed by the Driver and passenger of the vehicle the Plaintiff was occupying. The subject of the photos was identified as Deshawn Ford.

INTERROGATORY NO. 29:

Page 12 of 18




Identify each and every fact which supports the claim that the unknown driver was

inexperienced, careless or reckless.

ANSWER:

Plaintiff states the driver caused a motor vehicle collision and then fled the scene for unknown reasons and failing to render aid shows carelessness and recklessness.

INTERROGATORY NO. 30:

If any response to any of the attached Request for admissions is anything other than an unequivocal admission, please state the factual basis therefore.

ANSWER:

Objection, this interrogatory is stated as an instruction for the attached Request for

Admissions.

REQUESTS FOR ADMISSIONS

REQUEST NO. 1:

Admit that you have no facts to support the allegations that Virginia Sewell voluntarily provided her motor vehicle to the individual identified as “Unknown Driver”.

RESPONSE: Plaintiff states the allegation did not include the use or implication of ‘voluntarily’. The Plaintiff's complaint clearly stated “negligently” which infers to direct, indirect, intentional

and/or non-intentional action.

REQUEST NO. 2:

Admit that Virginia Sewell reported the vehicle owned by her as stolen on January 3, 2021. RESPONSE:

Plaintiff admits the vehicle was reported stolen on January 3, 2021 at 7:41pm, Nineteen

Page 13 of 18




(19) minutes after the accident was reported and officers were on the accident scene.

REQUEST NO. 3:

Admit that the motor vehicle owned by Virginia Sewell was not damaged as a result of the January 3, 2021, motor vehicle collision.

RESPONSE:

Objection, Plaintiff has no knowledge as to the condition of Defendant Sewell’s vehicle prior to the collision.

Without waiving said objection, Plaintiff states that per the previously referenced police report, there was ‘very minor’ damage to Defendant Sewell’s vehicle verifying the point of impact.

REQUEST N

Admit that Virginia Sewell had no reason to know/believe that the unknown vehicle operator

was inexperienced. RESPONSE:

Plaintiff states the ‘Unknown Driver’ was presented as Defendant Sewell’s significant other whom she would have intimate knowledge of.

REQUEST N

Admit that Virginia Sewell had no reason to know/believe that the party identified as “Unknown Driver” would drive the vehicle carelessly.

RESPONSE:

Plaintiff states the ‘Unknown Driver’ was presented as Defendant Sewell’s significant other whom she would have intimate knowledge of.

REQUEST N

Admit that Virginia Sewell had no reason to know/believe that the party identified as “Unknown Driver” would drive the vehicle recklessly.

Page 14 of 18




RESPONSE:

Plaintiff states the ‘Unknown Driver’ was presented as Defendant Sewell’s significant other whom she would have intimate knowledge of.

All photographs, negatives, drawings, or visual representations of the scene of the accident or vehicles involved in the subject accident.

RESPONSE:

Plaintiff states she was not the owner of the vehicle in which she was occupying and therefore, is not in possession of any photographs, negatives, drawings or visual representation of the scene of the accident or the vehicles involved.

RESPONSE:

Objection. Information regarding tax returns, including income tax returns, W-2

and/or 1099 forms, is privileged under federal and state law.

KENTUCKY UNIFORM POLICE TRAFFIC COLLISION REPORT - NARRATIVE ‘S00

1/2000

[MASTER FILE # 72581366

INVESTIGATING AGENCY LOUISVILLE METRO POLICE DEPT AGENCY ORI 0568000 LOCAL CODE [PHONE-398]

Officer arrived on scene of a reported injury accident where operator of Unit 1 fled the scene on foot and left the vehicle. Unit 2 was occupied three times. The rear passenger was taken to the hospital with possible injuries. Unit 2 driver and front passenger did not have operator licenses. Unit 2 operator was

cited under citation number DQ70306. Unit 1 operator was not on seen when police arrived. Officers located a photo of suspected male on social media of a male described as the subject that fled. The subject was identified by the driver and front passenger as an individual known to Unit 1 vehicle owner. Officers found out that the vehicle owner then made a stolen vehicle report for her vehicle while officers were on scene working the accident. Officers called Unit 1 vehicle owner and she stated she spoke with her boyfriend prior to filing the report for the stolen vehicle.

There was no damage to the vehicle's ignition and it being a push start would not allow the vehicle to start without a key. Officers spoke with the vehicle owner and she stated she only has one set of keys. Then she changed her statement when confronted about the ignition. She then stated she had a spare but has not been able to locate that key for a while.

Narrative

Dispatched code 3 on a MVA. Arrived on scene along with LMPD. 2 vehicles were involved, a white suv and a white sedan. Both vehicles did not appear to have any damage to them. The white sedan had 3 occupants that were female. The patient was a 20 year old female restrained passenger in the back seat. Patient was 37 weeks pregnant with her first child. Patient states that they were stopped at a stop sign when their vehicle got struck in the back by a white suv. The occupants in the suv jumped out a fled the scene. No airbag deployment in either vehicle. The patient stated that the car just shook. The patient denies head or neck pain. The patient states that she has been having lower back pain but just wants to make sure that nothing has happen to the baby because of the accident. Patient skin is pink, warm, and dry. Pupils are PERRL. Lung sounds are clear equal and bilateral. Patient has proper PMS function in all extremities. Patient abdomen is soft, non tender. Patient denies LOC, SOA, headache, dizziness, weakness, nausea, chest pain or abdomen pain. Patient vitals are within normal limits and are as noted. Patient requested transport to Baptist East Hospital for further evaluation. Transported code 1 to Baptist East Hospital. Continued to monitor patients vitals and condition without

remarkable changes. Arrived at Baptist East Hospital without any incidents. Transferred care to ED staff along with a verbal patient care report for further evaluation. All times are approximate.

BF oo ApTIST HEALTH’ Baptist Health Louisville Noble, Anella or 4000 Kresge Way MRN: [PHONE-195], DOB: 11/7/2000, Sex: F Louisville KY 40207-4605 Adm: 1/3/2021, D/C: 1/4/2021 [DOB-196] - ED to Hosp-Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH LOUISVILLE OBSTETRIC EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT (continued)

Care Plan (continued)

Disciplines: Nurse, Interdisciplinary Intervention: Identify and Manage Fall Risk Frequency: Per CPG Description: Perform standard risk assessment with a validated tool or comprehensive approach

appropriate to the patient on admission; reassess fall risk frequently, with change in status or transfer to another level of care.

Communicate fall injury risk to interprofessional healthcare team.

Determine need for increased observation, equipment and environmental modification, such as low bed and signage, as well as supportive, nonskid footwear.

Adjust safety measures to individual developmental age, stage and identified risk factors. Reinforce the importance of safety and physical activity with patient and family.

Perform regular intentional rounding to assess need for position change, pain assessment, personal needs, including assistance with toileting.

Intervention: Prevent Skin Injury

Frequency: Per CPG Description: Assess skin risk on admission and at regular intervals throughout hospital stay. Keep all areas of skin (especially folds) clean and dry. Maintain adequate skin hydration. Relieve and redistribute pressure and protect bony prominences; implement measures based on patient-specific risk factors. Match turning and repositioning schedule to clinical condition. Encourage weight shift frequently; assist with reposition if unable to complete independently. Float heels off bed. Avoid pressure on the Achilles tendon. Keep skin free from extended contact with medical devices. Use aids (e.g., slide boards, mechanical lift) during transfer.

Intervention: Prevent and Manage VTE (venous thromboembolism) Risk

Frequency: Per CPG Description: Assess for VTE risk. Encourage/assist with early ambulation. Initiate and maintain compression or other therapy, as indicated based on identified risk in accordance with organizational protocol/provider order. Encourage both active and passive leg exercises while in bed, if unable to ambulate.

Intervention: Prevent Infection

Frequency: Per CPG

Description: Maintain skin and mucous membrane integrity; promote hand, oral and pulmonary hygiene. Optimize fluid balance, nutrition, sleep and glycemic control to maximize infection resistance. Identify potential sources of infection early to prevent or mitigate progression of infection (e.g., wound, lines, devices). Evaluate ongoing need for invasive devices; remove promptly when no longer indicated.

Goal: Optimal Comfort and Wellbeing

Disciplines: Nurse, Interdisciplinary Intervention: Monitor Pain and Promote Comfort Frequency: Per CPG Description: Assess pain level, treatment efficacy and patient response at regular intervals using a

consistent pain scale.

Consider the presence and impact of preexisting chronic pain.

Encourage patient and caregiver involvement in pain assessment, interventions and safety measures.

Intervention: Provide Person-Centered Care

Frequency: Per CPG Description: Use a family-focused approach to care. Develop trust and rapport by proactively providing information, encouraging questions, addressing concerns and offering reassurance. Acknowledge emotional response to hospitalization. Printed on 4/20/21 8:15 AM Page 588




SF oo aPTIST HEALTH’ Baptist Health Louisville Noble, Anella or 4000 Kresge Way MRN: [PHONE-206], DOB: 11/7/2000, Sex: F Louisville KY 40207-4605 Adm: 1/3/2021, D/C: 1/4/2021 [DOB-198] - ED to Hosp-Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH LOUISVILLE OBSTETRIC EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT (continued)

Care Plan (continued)

Recognize and utilize personal coping strategies. Honor spiritual and cultural preferences.

Goal: Readiness for Transition of Care

Disciplines: Nurse, Interdisciplinary Intervention: Mutually Develop Transition Plan Frequency: Per CPG Description: Identify available resources for support (e.g., family, friends, community).

Identify and address barriers to ongoing treatment and home management (e.g., environmental, financial).

Provide opportunities to practice self-management skills.

Assess and monitor emotional readiness for transition.

Establish/reconnect linkage with outpatient providers or community-based services.

Point: Fall Prevention (Resolved)

Description:

The healthcare setting is an unfamiliar environment. Instruct the patient and family to call for help with activity to prevent a fall, even if feeling able to do things independently. Keep the room and pathway to bathroom clutter-free. Caution patient and family not to disconnect or silence any alarms.

Patient Friendly Description: We don't want you to fall.

Call for help, even if you feel like you can do things on your own. Keep the room and the path to bathroom clear.

Never disconnect or silence any alarms. Learning Progress Summary

Assessment Time: [DOB-257] 20:12:05

Dispatched code 3 on a MVA. Arrived on scene along with LMPD. 2 vehicles were involved, a white suv and a white sedan. Both vehicles did not appear to have any damage to them. The white sedan had 3 occupants that were female. The patient was a 20 year old female restrained passenger in the back seat. Patient was 37 weeks pregnant with her first child. Patient states that they were stopped at a stop sign when their vehicle got struck in the back by a white suv. The occupants in the suv jumped out a fled the scene. No airbag deployment in either vehicle. The patient stated that the car just shook. The patient denies head or neck pain. 2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL:

Physicians and certified registered nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. More Information

Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult

After a car accident (motor vehicle collision), it is common to have injuries to your head, face, arms, and body. These injuries may include:

Cuts.

Burns.

Bruises.

Sore muscles or a stretch or tear in a muscle (strain).

Headaches.

You may feel stiff and sore for the first several hours. You may feel worse after waking up the first morning after the accident. These injuries often feel worse for the first 24-48 hours. After that, you will usually begin to get better with each day. How quickly you get better often depends on:

How bad the accident was.

How many injuries you have. Where your injuries are.

What types of injuries you have. If you were wearing a seat belt. If your airbag was used.

A head injury may result in a concussion. This is a type of brain injury that can have serious effects. If you have a concussion, you should rest as told by your doctor. You must be very careful to avoid having a second concussion.

Follow these instructions at home: Medicines

e Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor. e If you were prescribed antibiotic medicine, take or apply it as told by your doctor. Do not stop using the antibiotic even if your condition gets better.

If you have a wound or a burn:

e Clean your wound or burn as told by your doctor. Wash it with mild soap and water. © Rinse it with water to get all the soap off. o Pat it dry with a clean towel. Do not rub it. © If you were told to put an ointment or cream on the wound, do so as told by your doctor. e Follow instructions from your doctor about how to take care of your wound or burn. Make sure you: o Know when and how to change or remove your bandage (dressing). o Always wash your hands with soap and water before and after you change your bandage. If you cannot use soap and water, use hand sanitizer. o Leave stitches (sutures), skin glue, or skin tape (adhesive) strips in place, if you have these. They may need to stay in place for 2 weeks or longer. If tape strips get loose and curl up, you may trim the loose edges. Do not remove tape strips completely unless your doctor says it is okay.

(e)

More Information (continued) ||

e Do not:

© Scratch or pick at the wound or burn. o Break any blisters you may have. © Peel any skin.

e Avoid getting sun on your wound or burn.

e Raise (e/evate) the wound or burn above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down. If you have a wound or burn on your face, you may want to sleep with your head raised. You may do this by putting an extra pillow under your head.

e Check your wound or burn every day for signs of infection. Check for:

© More redness, swelling, or pain. More fluid or blood. Warmth. Pus or a bad smell.

Oo 0 O

Activity

e Rest. Rest helps your body to heal. Make sure you: © Get plenty of sleep at night. Avoid staying up late. © Go to bed at the same time on weekends and weekdays. e Ask your doctor if you have any limits to what you can lift. e Ask your doctor when you can drive, ride a bicycle, or use heavy machinery. Do not do these activities if you are dizzy. e Ifyou are told to wear a brace on an injured arm, leg, or other part of your body, follow instructions from your doctor about activities. Your doctor may give you instructions about driving, bathing, exercising, or working.

General instructions

e If told, put ice on the injured areas. © Put ice in a plastic bag. = | ee | eek © Place a towel between your skin and the bag. a

© Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2—3 times a day. e Drink enough fluid to keep your pee (urine) pale yellow. e Do not drink alcohol. e Eat healthy foods. ¢ Keep all follow-up visits as told by your doctor. This is important.

Contact a doctor if:

Your symptoms get worse.

You have neck pain that gets worse or has not improved after 1 week.

You have signs of infection in a wound or burn.

You have a fever.

You have any of the following symptoms for more than 2 weeks after your car accident: o Lasting (chronic) headaches. © Dizziness or balance problems. o Feeling sick to your stomach (nauseous).

More sensitivity to noise or light.

Depression or mood swings.

Memory problems.

Trouble concentrating or paying attention.

Sleep problems.

Feeling tired all the time.

Get help right away if:

e You have: © Loss of feeling (numbness), tingling, or weakness in your arms or legs. Very bad neck pain, especially tenderness in the middle of the back of your neck. A change in your ability to control your pee or poop (stoo/). More pain in any area of your body. Swelling in any area of your body, especially your legs. Shortness of breath or light-headedness. Chest pain. Blood in your pee, poop, or vomit. Very bad pain in your belly (abdomen) or your back. Very bad headaches or headaches that are getting worse. o Sudden vision loss or double vision. e Your eye suddenly turns red. e The black center of your eye (pupil) is an odd shape or size.

oO0O000606UC0UdlUCOUlUCO

Summary

After a car accident (motor vehicle collision), it is common to have injuries to your head, face, arms, and body. Follow instructions from your doctor about how to take care of a wound or burn.

If told, put ice on your injured areas.

Contact a doctor if your symptoms get worse.

Keep all follow-up visits as told by your doctor.

This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you have with your health care provider.

Document Revised: [DOB-289] Document Reviewed: [DOB-290] Elsevier Patient Education © 2020 Elsevier Inc.

Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding

Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye

Sudden severe headache with no known cause

Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination

It is important to seek emergency care right away if you have further stroke symptoms. If you get

emergency help quickly, the powerful clot-dissolving medicines can reduce the disabilities caused by a stroke.

IF YOU SMOKE OR USE TOBACCO PLEASE READ THE FOLLOWING:

Why is smoking bad for me?

Smoking increases the risk of heart disease, lung disease, vascular disease, stroke, and cancer. If you smoke, STOP!

For more information:

Quit Now Kentucky 1-800-QUIT-NOW https://kentucky.quitlogix.org/en-US/

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: March 19, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 16 of 16 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder.

Low back pain, which she rated 5 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate. .

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 5 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5. Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain :

- Pain intensity: Previous: 3/10 Current: 3/10 Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Low Back Pain: - Pain intensity: Previous: 5/10 Current: 5/10

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Pain intensity: Previous: 5/10 Current: 5/10 Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

Diagnoses: * S16.1XXD Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon at neck level, Subsequent Encounter + M99.01 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of cervical region ¢ M54.13 Radiculopathy, cervicothoracic region + $39.012D Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon of low back, Subsequent Encounter *M99.03 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of lumbar region

* $46.911D Strain of unspecified muscle, fascia and tendon at shoulder and upper arm level, right arm, Subsequent Encounter

» M99.07 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of upper extremity (shoulder)

Plan

Spinal Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98940) was made to the following restricted spinal segments: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4, L5.

Upper Extremity Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98943) was made to the following restricted extremities: right shoulder.

Heat: Heat (97010) was applied to the Cervical, Lumbar for 15 minutes in order to increase bload flow to the area and relax the muscles.

Mechanical traction:

She was placed on an intersegmental traction table (97012) for 10 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement.

Hydrotherapy: She was placed on a hydromassage table (97039) for 15 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement.

Response to Treatment: Patient responded well to treatment and had no adverse reaction.

We will treat Ms. Noble as per the examination findings and continue the existing treatment plan. It is recommended that she return for treatment three times a week.

Hydrotherapy ~ 97039

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimentary in the treatment of many types of soft tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neurologic disorders as well as certain

post-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

- Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat

Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent Indication for the application of heat. Current thought

suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation.

e Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle

guarding. It also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in

treatment of post acute strains and sprains, Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment 0

and after long periods of immobilization.

e Decongestive — £ many types of injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites. » Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm.

healing rate) and resultant

e Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased

additional heat.

Physiological Effects of Massage

Increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints. increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, and peri-articular regions. Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding.

reased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of e Prevents adhesions and fibrosis in muscles ligaments and contiguous tissues.

» Decreased tendency towards muscle atrophy during long periods of immobilization or disuse.

Pain reduction and interruption of pain sensation cycle resulting in increased ease of mobility.

e Inc dema.

Patient Name: Anella Nobile Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: March 15, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 14 of 14 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 4 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder. Referring patient to MD. Ordering an cervical MRI: necessary due to consistent high levels of pain, patient's failure to respond to conservative treatment and possible ligament/disc injuries.

Low back pain, which she rated 7 out of 10, ona scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate. Ordering an lumbar MRI: necessary due to consistent high levels of pain, patient's failure to respond to conservative treatment and possible ligament/disc injuries.

Right shouider pain, which she rated 5 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5. Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of Jumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain :

- Pain intensity: Previous: 4/10 Current: 4/10 Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat

Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent indication for the application of heat. Current thought

suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation.

° Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle

guarding. [t also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in

treatment of post acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

»* Decongestive — Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment of many types of injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites.

Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm. Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

additional heat.

Physiological Effects of Massage

Increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints. Increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding.

Increased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of edema.

Prevents adhesions and fibrosis in muscles ligaments and contiguous tissues.

« Decreased tendency towards muscle atrophy during long periods of immobilization or disuse, uction and interruption of pain sensation cycle resulting in increased ease of mobility.

Ortho/Neuro Exam:

An evaluation (CPT code 99212) was performed on Ms. Noble today, using medical decision making as the determining factor. The number and complexity of problems addressed was straightforward and the amount and/or complexity of data to be reviewed and analyzed was minimal or none. The exam consisted of visual assessment of range of motion, manual muscle tests, deep tendon reflexes, dermatomal sensation, orthopedic

tests and palpation.

Exam Findings: Cervical Spine

Ortho Cervical The following orthopedic test(s) for the cervical spine were performed:

Forminal Compression Test: Produced radicular symptoms in the right upper extremity.

bilaterally and T1 bilaterally.

Injury Causation

In my opinion, based on the history and my evaluation, the injuries suffered by Ms. Noble are a direct result of the

motor vehicle collision of [DOB-322].

According to the article, "A practicable and systematic approach to medicolegal causation,” rules for assessing potential causal relationships have been formalized in the form of the “Hill criteria.” The Hill criteria is broken down to 3 basic elements for practical application in clinical assessments of causation.

A recent legal decision from the 10th Circuit US Court of Appeals endorsed the 3-step causal methodology as the generally accepted approach for injury causation.

4. Plausibility. This first step addresses whether it is biologically possible for the injury event to have caused the condition. Epidemiologic and other scientific literature can serve as a basis for a determination of plausibility, but clinical experience is also an adequate basis for the determination. It is appropriate to use prior clinical experience with an injury mechanism, gleaned from patient histories, as a foundation for assessing whether an injury plausibly resulted from a similar injury mechanism.

2. Temporality. This second step, which examines the clinical and other evidence of the timing between the onset of the symptoms of injury and the injury event, must be satisfied to assess the specific cause of the patient's injury. First, it must be established that the sequence of the injury and the event is appropriate; the symptoms cannot be identically present prior to the event. Further, the onset of the symptoms of injury cannot be implausibly latent, relative to the injury event.

3. Lack of a more probable alternative explanation. This final step is akin to a differential etiology in that the probability of alternative explanations is assessed and weighed relative to the injury risk of the traumatic event in question. Any evidence of an intervening injury event must be evaluated as the most obvious competing explanation. The estimation of the likelihood of the competing explanation can come from clinical experience, epidemiologic study, or a combination of sources.

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimen d neurologic disorders as well as certain

tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, an

post-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent indication for the application of heat. Current thought

suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation. Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle guarding. It also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in

st acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: January 25, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 10 of 10 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder. Baby due anytime.

Low back pain, which she rated 6 out of 10, ona scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A- Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5. Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain:

- Pain intensity: Previous: 3 Current: 3

Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Low Back Pain: - Pain intensity: Previous: 6 Current: 6

The Injury Centers, 2137 Dixie Highway, Louisville, KY 40210 Phone: [PHONE-336]

Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Shoulder Pain:

- Pain intensity: Previous: 3 Current: 3

Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Diagnoses: * $16.1XXD Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon at neck level, Subsequent Encounter * M99.01 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of cervical region * M54.13 Radiculopathy, cervicothoracic region + $39.012D Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon of low back, Subsequent Encounter + M99.03 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of lumbar region

* $46.911D Strain of unspecified muscle, fascia and tendon at shoulder and upper arm level, right arm, Subsequent Encounter

* M99.07 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of upper extremity (shoulder)

Plan

Spinal Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98940) was made to the following restricted spinal segments: C5, C6, C7, L3, 14, L5.

Upper Extremity Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98943) was made to the following restricted extremities: right shoulder. Heat: Heat (97010) was applied to the Cervical, Lumbar for 15 minutes in order to increase blood flow to the area and relax the muscles. Mechanical traction: She was placed on an intersegmental traction table (97012) for 10 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement.

Hydrotherapy: She was placed on a hydromassage table (97039) for 15 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement.

Response to Treatment: Patient responded well to treatment and had no adverse reaction.

Low back pain, which she rated 5 out of 10, ona scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 40 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5.

Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very com

tissue injuries and other condit t-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

pos

Hydrotherapy — 97039

plimentary in the treatment of many types of soft

ions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neu rologic disorders as well as certain

Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat

Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent indication for the application of heat. Current thought

suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation.

Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle

guarding. It also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in

treatment of post acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

Decongestive — Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment of many types of injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites. Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm.

Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

additional heat.

Physiological Effects of Massage

Increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints. Increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, and peri-articular regions.

Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding. Increased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of edema.

Prevents adhesions and fibrosis in muscles ligaments and contiguous tissues.

Decreased tendency towards muscle atrophy during long periods of immobilization or disuse.

Pain reduction and interruption of pain sensation cycle resulting in increased ease of mobility.

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: January 14, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 7 of 7 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder.

Low back pain, which she rated 7 out of 10, ona scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 4 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5. Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain :

- Pain intensity: Previous: 3 Current: 3

Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

Hydrotherapy — 97039

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimentary in the treatment of many types of soft tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neurologic disorders as well as certain post-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat

Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent indication for the application of heat. Current thought

suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation.

Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle guarding. It also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in treatment of post acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

Decongestive — Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment of many types of Injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites.

Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm.

Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

additional heat,

Physiological Effects of Massage

Increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints.

Increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, and peri-articular regions. Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding.

increased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of edema.

Prevents adhesions and fibrosis in muscles ligaments and contiguous tissues.

Decreased tendency towards muscle atrophy during long periods of immobilization or disuse. Pain reduction and interruption of pain sensation cycle resulting in increased ease of mobility.

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: January 11, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 5 of 5 Subjective

P . Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder.

Low back pain, which she rated 6 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and LS.

Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain :

- Pain intensity: Previous: 3 Current: 3

Pain intensity remained the same.

- Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Low Back Pain: - Pain intensity: Previous: 6 Current: 6

* $46.911D Strain of unspecified muscle, fascia and tendon at shoulder and upper arm level, right arm, Subsequent Encounter

Plan

Mechanical traction: She was placed on an intersegmental traction table (97012) for 10 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement. Hydrotherapy: She was placed on a hydromassage table (97039) for 15 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement. Response to Treatment: Patient responded well to treatment and had no adverse reaction.

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimentary in the treatment of many types of soft

tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neurologic disorders as well as certain post-surgical conditions, These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

eduction in muscle

guarding. treatment of post acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites. e Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm. Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

Physiological Effects of Massage

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient’s DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: January 6, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 3 of 3 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

Ms. Noble presented to the office today with the following complaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 400% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder.

Low back pain, which she rated 6 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Right shoulder pain, which she rated 3 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This symptom occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate.

Objective

A - Asymmetry/Misalignment Restrictions were noted at the following spinal levels: C5, C6, C7, L3, L4 and L5.

Upper extremity restrictions were noted in the right shoulder.

R - Range of Motion Abnormality

A visual assessment of cervical range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of lumbar range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: flexion, extension, left lateral flexion, right lateral flexion, left rotation and right rotation. A visual assessment of shoulder range of motion revealed an apparent limitation and an increase in pain in the following planes of motion: right abduction and right adduction.

T - Tissue/Tone Changes

Muscle spasms were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae, right rhomboid and bilateral erector spinae.

Myofascial trigger points were noted in the following muscles: right trapezius, right levator scapulae and bilateral erector spinae.,

Muscle guarding was noted in the following muscles: bilateral lumbar paraspinal.

Assessment

Neck Pain :

- Pain intensity: Previous: 5 Current: 3

Pain intensity improved by 40% from previous visit. - Pain frequency: Previous: 100% Current: 100% Pain frequency remained the same.

- Acute (< 4 weeks since onset)

Low Back Pain: - Pain intensity: Previous: 7 Current: 6

Diagnoses: * $16.1XXD Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon at neck level, Subsequent Encounter * M99.01 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of cervical region * M54.13 Radiculopathy, cervicothoracic region * $39.012D Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon of low back, Subsequent Encounter * M99.03 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of lumbar region

» $46.911D Strain of unspecified muscle, fascia and tendon at shoulder and upper arm level, right arm, Subsequent Encounter

+ M99.07 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of upper extremity (shoulder)

Plan

Spinal Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98940) was made to the following restricted spinal segments: C5, C6, C7, 13, L4, L5.

Upper Extremity Adjustments: Chiropractic manipulative therapy (98943) was made to the following restricted extremities: right shoulder. Heat: Heat (97010) was applied to the Cervical, Lumbar for 15 minutes in order to increase blood flow to the area and relax the muscles. Mechanical traction: She was placed on an intersegmental traction table (97012) for 10 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement. Hydrotherapy: She was placed on a hydromassage table (97039) for 15 minutes in order to promote muscle relaxation and improve circulation and intersegmental movement.

Response to Treatment: Patient responded well to treatment and had no adverse reaction.

Hydrotherapy — 97039

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimentary in the treatment of many types of soft tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neurologic disorders as well as certain post-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

Physiologic Effects of Radiant Heat

Analgesic — This effect is the most frequent indication for the application of heat. Current thought

° suggests this effect is related to the gate control theory of pain modulation.

e Antispasmodic — Heat is generally considered to produce a relaxation effect and reduction in muscle guarding. It also increases the elasticity of connective tissue which is an important consideration in treatment of post acute strains and sprains, and after long periods of immobilization.

e Decongestive ~ Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment of many types of injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites. e Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm. Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

additional heat.

Physiological Effects of Massage

increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints.

Increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, and peri-articular regions. Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding.

Increased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of edema.

Prevents adhesions and fibrosis in muscles ligaments and contiguous tissues.

Decreased tendency towards muscle atrophy during long periods of immobilization or disuse, Pain reduction and interruption of pain sensation cycle resulting in increased ease of mobility.

The Physiological effects of heat and massage are very complimentary in the treatment of many types of soft tissue injuries and other conditions such as orthopedic, rheumatic, and neurologic disorders as well as certain post-surgical conditions. These two forms of therapy are therefore frequently applied together.

e Decongestive — Increased capillary blood flow is important in the treatment of many types of injury

addition to an increased clearing of metabolites. e Sedative — Heat helps decrease spasticity, tenderness and spasm. Local Vasodialation — Increases local metabolic rate (increased healing rate) and resultant

additional heat.

Physiological Effects of Massage

increases local blood supply to soft tissues, muscles and joints.

Increased drainage and reduction of swelling in soft tissue, muscle, and peri-articular regions. e Muscle relaxation and reduction in muscle guarding.

Increased venous and lymphatic return augmenting reduction of edema.

Patient Name: Anella Noble Date of onset: January 3, 2021 Patient's DOB: [DOB-2] Date of visit: January 4, 2021 Doctor's Name: Robert Black, DC Visit #: 1 of 1 Subjective

P - Pain/Tenderness

PI History: Ms. Noble presented to the office today for evaluation of injuries she sustained in a motor vehicle collision on January 3, 2021. Rear Ended. She reported that she was the restrained right rear passenger of a 2012 Ford Fusion that was traveling at an unknown speed when it was struck at the rear by an unknown year, make, and model vehicle that was traveling at an unknown speed. The patient noted that the airbag did not deploy. Ms. Noble also reported that she did not lose

consciousness.

Mechanism of Injury: The probability that Ms. Noble was injured in the collision may be increased due to the following factors: Patient Surprised by Impact: Ms. Noble reported that she was unaware of the impending collision. According to Mertz and Patrick, the unaware occupant is at a greater risk of injury. (Mertz HJ, Patrick LM. Investigation of the kinematics and kinetics of whiplash. 1967; SAE 670919.)

Rear-End Collision with Seatbelt: Ms. Noble reported that her seatbelt was fastened at the time of the collision. According to Allen, Barnes and Bodiwala, shoulder belts are very effective at saving lives in auto accidents, but there is some evidence that they can actually cause more damage in a rear end collision. Because the body is held in place, the neck suffers worse hyperflexion. The cervical spine may also undergo a twisting motion from the head restraint, causing a more complex injury. (Allen MJ, Barnes MR, Bodiwala GG. The effect of seat belt legislation on injuries sustained by car occupants. Injury: The British Journal of Accident Surgery 1985; 16; 471-476.)

Immediate Pain: Ms. Noble reported that she felt Low back pain immediately after the collision. A study by Radanov found that patients who reported pain immediately after their accidents were more likely to have pain at two years post-injury. It is generally recognized that patients with immediate symptoms are at a higher risk of long-term pain from whiplash. (Radanov BP, Sturzenegger M, De Stefano G. Long-term outcome after whiplash injury. A two-year follow-up considering the features of injury mechanisms and somatic, radiologic and psychosocial findings. Medicine 1995; 74(5): 281-296.)

Ms. Nobie presented to the office today with the following compiaints:

Right neck pain, which she rated 5 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This pain occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble reported that the onset was gradual and began ago. She reported that the right neck pain was due to a motor vehicle collision on 1/3/2021. She noted that her neck is aggravated by bending her neck forward, bending her neck backward, tilting her head to the left, tilting her head to the right, turning her head to the left and turning her head to the right and relieved by nothing. She described the quality of pain as sharp, achy, nagging, shooting and stiff. Ms. Noble noted that the pain is unaffected by time of day. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom radiates to the right shoulder. Ms. Noble denied a history of prior treatment for this symptom. The patient reported that the current symptom was not present prior to this injury.

Functional Assessment: Functional Rating Index: 48/100

Low back pain, which she rated 7 out of 10, on a scale from 0 to 10, with 10 being the worst. This pain occurs 100% of her awake time. Ms. Noble reported that the onset was sudden and began ago. She reported that the low back pain was due to a motor vehicle collision on 1/3/2021. She noted that her back is aggravated by bending forward at her waist, bending backward at her waist, tilting left at her waist, tilting right at her waist, twisting left at her waist, twisting right at her waist, standing, sitting, lying down and lying on side in bed and relieved by nothing. She described the quality of pain as sharp, achy, deep, nagging and stiff. Ms. Noble noted that the pain is worse at night. Ms. Noble noted that this symptom does not radiate. Ms. Noble reported that she recently received the following treatment for the back:. The patient reported that the current symptom was not present prior to this injury. Baptist Health ER by EMS (1/03/2021).

Injury Causation

In my opinion, based on the history and my evaluation, the injuries suffered by Ms. Noble are a direct result of the

motor vehicle collision of [DOB-393].

According to the article, "A practicable and systematic approach to medicolegal causation," rules for assessing potential causal relationships have been formalized in the form of the “Hill criteria.” The Hill criteria is broken down to 3 basic elements for practical application in clinical assessments of causation.

A recent legal decision from the 10th Circuit US Court of Appeals endorsed the 3-step causal methodology as the

generally accepted approach for injury causation.

4. Plausibility. This first step addresses whether it is biologically possible for the injury event to have caused the condition. Epidemiologic and other scientific literature can serve as a basis for a determination of plausibility, but clinical experience is also an adequate basis for the determination. It is appropriate to use prior clinical experience with an injury mechanism, gleaned from patient histories, as a foundation for assessing whether an injury plausibly resulted from a similar injury mechanism.

2. Temporality. This second step, which examines the clinical and other evidence of the timing between the onset of the symptoms of injury and the injury event, must be satisfied to assess the specific cause of the patient's injury. First, it must be established that the sequence of the injury and the event is appropriate; the symptoms cannot be identically present prior to the event. Further, the onset of the symptoms of injury cannot be

implausibly latent, relative to the injury event.

3. Lack of a more probable alternative explanation. This final step is akin to a differential etiology in that the probability of alternative explanations is assessed and weighed relative to the injury risk of the traumatic event in question. Any evidence of an intervening injury event must be evaluated as the most obvious competing explanation. The estimation of the likelinood of the competing explanation can come from clinical experience, epidemiologic study, or a combination of sources.

Freeman MD. A practicable and systematic approach to medicolegal causation. Orthopedics 2018;41(2):70-2. With regards to this specific case, the issue of causation was determined based on the following information:

1. Biologic Plausibility - in my opinion, it is biologically possible that the injuries sustained by Ms. Noble were caused

by the motor vehicle collision of [DOB-394].

2. Temporality - Ms. Noble’s symptoms began on or after the motor vehicle collision noted above.

3. Lack of a More Probable Alternative Explanation: Based on the history as reported by Ms. Noble, there are no more probable alternative explanations that could account for the injuries noted.

Diagnoses: * $16.1XXA Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon at neck level, Initial Encounter * M99.01 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of cervical region * M54.13 Radiculopathy, cervicothoracic region « $39.012A Strain of muscle, fascia and tendon of low back, Initial Encounter * M99.03 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of lumbar region

* $46.911A Strain of unspecified muscle, fascia and tendon at shoulder and upper arm level, right arm, Initial Encounter

* M99.07 Segmental and somatic dysfunction of upper extremity (shoulder)
